My throat surgeon put me on a schedule of drinking organic lemon juice(whole lemon juiced) into 4 ozs of room temp distilled water in the morning and again at night before bed.  This will make your body basic in 30 days.  This is what you want to make the cancer cells die.  Cancer cells cannot live in a non-acidic environment.  I did this when I was 27 and now I'm 58 and still cancer free!!!!  Wishing you two the best for the rest of your lives!!!!   Live Well, Love Much, Stay Positive, and Laugh Each and Every Day!!!! Wow, we have been waiting 3 weeks to hear from you all, and you knocked it out of the park !  First, Becs, so good to see you sweetie, know you have been going thru quite a journey and we can still see the strong spirit in you !  Ok, 2nd, Eamon, you are a rock hard builder genius. You take your visions and you have amazing ability to visualize and make things happen and the new porch room is simply Rock tabulis. 3rd, You both have fab dab amazing family bringing their work ethic and enthusiasm and love to both of you, so kuddos to them.  And 4thly !  I have said this before to others and will share it to you Both...Caretaking is just as Hard !  It's about as hard as having the actual illness, and I don't mean to denigrate the challenges that Bec is facing, but Caretakers have to be strong for the care-takee, plus themselves, plus others around you. Trust me, as one in your shoes a couple of times, "Control" is the toughest thing you will face.  As a kinda control freak myself, I made myself crazy with trying to control everything...doctors..meds, foods, schedules, just the whole rollercoaster of everyday things, and finally, a very wise nurse educated me to the fact, that we can't control everything, no matter how hard we try and that this is perfect example of "pick your battles". Once I understood that and put it into practice, my attitude really changed and was better mentally for me and the ones who were sick around me, and she basically taught me to give myself a break...and give my loved one a break...it is a rollercoaster and some days are going to be good, and some days more challenging. And, that it is OKay, to admit when one is struggling, and to reach out for help and understanding...it is OKay for the caretakee to admit when things are not that great, and to give "them" as much control as they can manage - so example, Becs is not that hungry, but you want her to have nutrition, and you give her this Big plate of food goodies thinking it will be good, when all she can think is "ugh"...so you do it on a smaller scale, give her  small plate with just maybe 5 0r 6 bites that she can choose from...if she just wants ice-cream, again, give her some, on a small scale.  She needs to sleep the whole day away? Cool, let her, and just check in once in a while. Becs, when you want to be "involved" on the build and not really energetic to actually do much, just grab a seat for a bit and be the audience and cheerleader squad for the process. Small steps are important. I am sorry to go on so long here, but from what I went thru, I feel it is my mission to help others have a bit better time because of my own experience.  And 5thly, "Osso", that Pup came to you in perfect time to give you joy, humor and love ğŸ¥°, and those scenes of him jumping on that couch as you were trying to move it out, were the funniest, laugh out loud moments I have experienced for a long time.  Hang in there ya'all, and Keep Breathing ğŸ˜˜

During a very very hard and traumatizing time in my life I was having some sort of vulnerable conversation with my father. At some point I told him that I am striving to be a rock. I wish I could quote the exact words but its been too long. He told me to be a tree. A rock is not as as strong as we believe. Its under pressure, it is limited to movevemwnt and growth, and that the more the rock goes through the more life chips if away. He told me to be a tree. A tree can go through so many hardships but it keeps adapting and growing. If may be missing a limb or have a scare, but despite everything it keeps growing/living.   During stressful times I love to get out into nature of be near trees or other plants. I find them so grounding. ğŸ’š

Just a bit of information that most people aren't aware of, if Bec or any of you have to get a blood draw, ask the technician to only take half vials or quarter vials.   The majority of your immune system is in your blood and blood draws effectively remove part of your immune system so the less they take, the better.  They only need a small amount for tests and the rest gets thrown away. Sending you guys lots of love and support.

I have walked many miles in those same shoes Eamon. As guys, we seem to often be hardwired to be "fixers". If something isn't right we fix it, if it's broken, we fix it, if it's just not working, we fix it. And we get used to that role and comfortable with that attitude of being able to control situations by "fixing" something. When my wife and I began OUR cancer journey, one of the hardest things for me was learning to accept that I was indeed powerless to "FIX" anything. It is amazingly hard to look at someone you love suffering something as difficult as chemo and be entirely powerless to make it better. The feelings of not being able to do anything to make it better are terrible to deal with, BUT, learning to accept that I had no control over it but could still be strong and supportive in the face of it was a big step in my personal growth. It's no fun man, but find ways to be who Bec needs you to be. make a special dessert, or find a special hat or warm fuzzy gift. You're creative and resourceful, and THAT can be your current superpower! I know you have the inner strength ! Celebrate the good days, endure the hard days, and remember EVERY day is a VICTORY! Love and prayers to both of you!

When my daughter had cancer I let my mind go to those dark places until I got the right help.  Everytime it starts to go there stop and take inventory on reality.  Bec isn't dead, you aren't at the funeral, stop imagining what it would be like without her etc. I know all the dark places. Imagine sealing a door behind them and put yourself into your safe place. Say in your mind, going to your safe place now and mentally go there. While you are in your safe place repeat "The future hasn't happened, I can't change the past, the only time you really have is the amount of time it takes for me to look into your eyes and you look back." It's always had to live in the moment, but if you live in the future and past you will miss the current moment. Love you guys. Take care of your self Eamon. Care giver stress is real and will wipe you out as fast as the chemo wipes out Bec.
